"Hi, Johnny,"


a sweet, familiar voice said. Beatrice walked over with a bright smile that looked so natural.


Johnny's mood instantly lifted. That smile always worked on him.


"Are you here to study?"


"Mm-hmm." she nodded. "Exams are coming up, sol need to put in the extra hours."


Something about that reminded Johnny of Grace's question. "Do you study at home every day?" he asked suddenly. "You haven't... been going out or eating with anyone else, have you?"


Usually, Beatrice could've handled such questions with ease-made up some sweet excuse or laughed it off.

But after overhearing his talk with Grace, his questions instantly made her uneasy.


Guilt pressed down on her chest, and suddenly,every word he said felt like it was hiding a deeper meaning-like he was testing her without saying it outright.


She forced her nerves down and gave him a soft,practiced smile. "The exams are so close-l've been locked in with my books at home. I want to get into the best university in the city."


She even tilted her head and blinked sweetly,looking completely innocent.


The moment Johnny saw that face, any doubts he had vanished. He didn't question her further. Instead,he mentally scolded himself for listening to Grace's nonsense.



The Beatrice he knew, even with her modest upbringing, was hardworking and fulI of drive. Her smile could light up a room, and she always seemed genuinely kind. She'd often ask him to tag along to buy snacks and feed the stray cats and dogs.


There was no way a girl like her was mixed up with shady older men. Grace was probably just trying to stir things up-or maybe she'd gotten it all wrong!


Feeling guilty for ever questioning Beatrice, Johnny reached out and gently took her hand. "Would you tutor me sometime? I want to get into the same university."


The meaning behind his words was clear-he wanted to stay with her, even after graduation.


This love-struck boy would stay wNrapped around her finger, offering whatever support he could.


He didn't handle the family money, but he saved faithfully, and while it wasn't nearly as much as what she got from other men, it still added up.


Plus, he was good-looking, and his family name carried weight. He might not have much now,but he was bound to be wealthy someday. It was just a shame his mother was so tightfisted, never givinghim enough allowance.


Still, Beatrice planned to keep him close while quietly getting what she needed from other men.


For now, she tucked those thoughts away and gave a shy smile. "But my grades aren't as good as Gianna's. Wouldn't it be better to ask her instead?"


Of course, she didn't mean it. It was just part of her act.
###Chapter 80 Lost To The Same Person
Johnny immediately shook his head and said, "I don't want Gianna tutoring me.I only want you."


Though he and Gianna were related, their relationship had always been shallow, more for appearances than genuine connection. There was hardly any interaction between them outside formal occasions.


Johnny was well aware that Gianna, proud and self-assured, respected his brother solely because of his talent and status.



But when it came to him, she barely hid her disdain.Even though they were classmates, he had gotten in through his father's influence, while Gianna had earned her spot through sheer merit. That fact only deepened her contempt.


"Alright, if I have time after school, I'll tutor you,"Beatrice replied, her warm smile lighting up her face. Lately, she'd had a minor falling-out with her benefactor, which left her with time to spare.Entertaining Johnny was convenient-and it didn't hurt to keep him dangling.


Her smile was gentle and reassuring, the kind that soothed Johnny's restless heart. That was also part of the reason he was so drawn to her.






After leaving the library, Grace had planned to take a taxi home.


She had already let Julia know she'd be staying late to study, so there was no need for her to come pick her up.


Julia had responded with a flurry of cheerful emojis,even promising to make Grace a special dinner that night.


Grace thought about how Julia always insisted she eat more, which could be a bit much at times.


She wasn't trying to diet, and her fast metabolism meant she never gained weight easily. Still, her appetite had always been modest.


Just as she stepped through the school gate, a sleek,top-of-the-line Lamborghini glided to a stop in front of her.


It was a newly released model, with only three of its kind in the world. Grace, being a motorsport enthusiast, had followed its debut closely.


But considering her current role as a hardworking student, she'd set aside her dream of owning a car for the time being.


Now,seeing one up close, it was hard to look away.


What stunned her even more was the person stepping out of the car-it was none other than Colton.


"What a coincidence, we meet again," he said smoothly.


"What are you doing here?" Grace asked, lifting an eyebrow. "The anniversary of my alma mater is coming up,"Colton explained with ease. "The principal called personally and invited me to attend."


Grace found that odd. Someone like him didn't need to show up just to accept an invitation. "So why come in person now?" she asked, curious despite herself.



"I just finished discussing a few things with the principal," he replied casually.


"Alright," she said, not bothering to ask what they talked about. Business matters never interested her.


"Are you heading home? Let me give you a ride,"Colton offered, his tone leaving little room for refusal."You saved my life once. Offering you a lift is the least | can do."


He had gone out of his way to be considerate, and it would feel rude to turn him down. Besides, it spared her the effort of hailing a taxi-something her naturally lazy side welcomed.
So,without hesitation, Grace slid into the passenger seat.


As the car pulled away, Lizzie exclaimed, "Gianna,look. Grace Miller sure moves fast-looks like she's switched men again!"


Just moments earlier, Lizzie and Gianna had witnessed Grace stepping into a sleek, unfamiliar car with a man.



They hadn't seen his face-he had his back to them -but his towering height, commanding presence,and refined attire spoke volumes.


Even from behind, he radiated sophistication. And that car-flashy and impossible to miss-was in a league of its own.


"She's always had a flirtatious streak," Gianna replied, her voice calm, her face emotionless.Yet her words dripped with venom, betraying the irritation bubbling beneath her composed surface. "Given her lowly background, it's not surprising. Clinging to wealthy men is probably her way of running from the past."


"What a shame! Her cumulative scandals would seriously damage the Holden family's reputation if they were made public," Lizzie said, wanting to win Gianna over because she knew she didn't like Grace.



Gianna said nothing, but the frustration twisting in her chest was difficult to ignore.


Whether it was the recent exams or Terry's endorsement, she had lost-to the same person every time. Grace.


Even Ellie, her teacher, now seemed to harbor quiet regret over the choices she'd made.


Time after time, Gianna found Grace stood in her way, stealing the spotlight and pushing her further into the shadows.


But it didn't matter. With the upcoming anniversary celebration on the horizon, a wave of alumni-now influential figures in various fields-would be returning.
Rumor had it the head of the Pearson family would be among them. That meant the game wasn't over yet. She still had a chance. A chance to step on Grace and rise again in a blaze of glory.






"I've made a patch of Rejuvenation PilI. I'll bring some to you next time," Grace said suddenly, her voice steady as they drove through the city.


Thanks to Colton's support, Eliana no longer had to wait in frustration.


Grace never liked owing favors. Giving him some pills felt like a fair return-with a little interest.


After all, she'd earned far more from their last deal than she had ever expected.
###Chapter 81 Whose Enemy
"Next time? And when exactly will that be?"


Colton wasn't just making small talk-he wanted a solid answer. With Grace, things could easily be dragged out for weeks.


To Grace, it sounded like he was just eager to get his hands on the pills.


"There's no rush. The poison's already cleared from your system. Your body's back to normal. Whether you take those pills or not won't really make a difference now."


Colton didn't drop the subject. "So? When are you planning to give them to me?"


"Saturday sounds good? I don't have any classes then, so I can bring the pills to you myself," Grace said, her lips curving slightly. He really wasn't patient.
"Saturday's fine. Bring me the pils and I'll treat you to a meal." He added the offer as if it were no big deal, but that last part mattered more to him than he let on.



Grace didn't turn him down. Those pills didn't come cheap,and in return, a meal was a small ask.


After that, the conversation quieted. Neither of them was big on small talk, and the silence inside the car settled in fast-calm, still, almost eerie.


But Colton was used to silence. Being reserved and distant was second nature to him. Sitting quietly like this didn't feel strange at all.


Then they both noticed it. A car was following them.


Neither of them said anything. Instead, they both subtly glanced at the rearview mirror.


Colton pressed harder on the gas, hoping to lose the car behind them, but it was no use-the ones tailing them were skilled trackers. They were sticking close without letting up.
Colton's calm gave way to irritation. "Hold on," he muttered, and with a sharp twist of the wheel,the car jerked forward, swerving and drifting through traffic with practiced skill.


But the pursuers didn't back off. They matched him move for move and even rammed into the back of his car.



Even though Colton's car was reinforced and bulletproof, the vehicle chasing them was just as tough-clearly built for this kind of job.



Grace quickly realized this wasn't some random ambush. These people had serious, powerful backing.


Could it be the so-called "Devil" from the northern faction? Had they finally tracked her down?


Even though there were two factions, they all came from the same core organization, which made it hard to tell whether the attackers were from the southern faction or the northern faction.

 Only the person who gave the order would know for sure.



Colton's mind was going through the same possibilities. If his cover had been blown, maybe the southern faction had finally made a move to get rid of him.



Whoever they were, it was impossible to figure out right now. And with the chase getting more intense by the second, the only option left was to face them head-on.


Colton's car, built for speed and power, held its own with ease, making it tough for the pursuers to gain the upper hand.


They didn't care about crashing or about damage-they were clearly here to finish the job.


Out of nowhere, another car appeared, cutting them off and forcing Colton toward the edge of a narrow bridge.


There was no time to think. Jumping out would be

the safest option.


"Jump now!" Grace shouted, throwing the door open and leaping without waiting for his reply.


Colton reacted instantly. Before she even landed, he grabbed her mid-air and shielded her with his body as they tumbled down the embankment.


Thankfully, they hit soft grass instead of concrete,rolling roughly but escaping with just a few scrapes.


Above them, the two black cars didn't stop or check -they made a sharp U-turn and sped away,disappearing without a trace.


The way they moved-fast, focused, and without hesitation-made it clear they were professionally trained.


There was no doubt about it now-they had been sent by someone high up in the ranks.


Grace's calm gaze sharpened, a flicker of anger rising beneath the surface, while Colton's eyes narrowed, dark and dangerous.
"What just happened?" he asked. "I'm always direct with people. I don't have enemies. Are you sure this wasn't meant for you?" Colton played it cool, acting like he had nothing to do with it, casually trying to shift the blame onto Grace.



"I'm just a student," she replied, eyes wide with innocence."Why would I have enemies?"


Colton raised an eyebrow. "Right. A simple student.Not an underground miracle healer with a secret side job?"


"And you, Mr. Pearson, a company president with power and connections-shouldn't you be the one with a longer enemy list?" Grace shot back, not missing a beat.


Neither of them said it out loud, but the same thought ran through their minds. "This attack was meant for me-it had to be someone from the other side."


They held back from admitting it, worried that saying too much might expose who they really were.
Still, deep down, they both were sure those people hadn't shown up by chance. They were the targets.


"You're hurt. Let me take you to the hospital," Colton said as his eyes landed on the red scrapes scattered across Grace's arms.



They weren't deep, but they stood out-and for some reason, that made him feel strangely unsettled.


As for the southern faction, he fully intended to make them pay for it!


"No need. I'm a doctor. I'll clean it up and apply some ointment at home." Unfortunately, she hadn't brought any of her medicine today-if she had, the wounds would've started healing within hours.



Grace was already in a bad mood, and the thought of her mother seeing the scrapes and getting all worried only made it worse.


She clenched her fists slightly. She would never let go of the attackers from the northern faction. This wouldn't be forgotten.

 "No." Colton gave her just one firm word before pulling out his phone and calling Dominick to come pick them up and head to the nearest hospital.


Somehow, the assistant showed up almost instantly,proving that Colton was even more capable than she'd guessed, with a sharp, well-prepared team always at his side.
###Chapter 82 Not Dating





After having her scrapes patched up at the hospital,Grace ducked into the restroom for a moment.



Ready to rejoin Colton and leave, she spun on her heel, only to hear a voice she recognized instantly,thick with tears.



"Grace! Oh, my darling! Are you alright? I was worried sick!"



Julia's sudden appearance left Grace momentarily stunned. The evidence of her mother's sobbing was unmistakable-red, swollen eyes and an emotional disarray that spoke of minutes spent weeping.


Standing close by, Rodger looked equally stricken,anxiety carved into every line of his face.



Grace tried to offer a reassuring smile. "I'm okay,really.How did you find me here?"
"How could we not come the minute we heard about your car accident? It terrified us! I can't tell you how relieved I am to see you safe!"


Just hearing the news of Grace's crash had nearly sent Julia into a faint.


Fresh tears glimmered as Julia scanned Grace from head to toe, unable to hide her distress at the sight of those shallow, red marks on her daughter's skin.


"Mom, honestly, it's nothing-just a few scratches,"Grace assured her gently.


Rodger's concern deepened as he pressed the issue."Are you absolutely certain? I really think it's best for you to get a thorough examination. Sometimes injuries hide beneath the surface and only reveal themselves much later. What if something starts bothering you after we've already left? That's what worries me the most."



Nodding vigorously, Julia echoed his concern. "He's absolutely right! Let's have a doctor check you out from head to toe right away," she insisted. Any amount of waiting or extra cost was a small price for knowing Grace was truly alright.


Reaching for his phone, Rodger was ready to call a doctor, but Grace reached out and stopped him in his tracks.



"No need to worry, really-I know my own health better than anyone. Don't forget, medicine is my field," she insisted with a gentle but confident smile.


To prove her point, she spun around lightly and even bounced on her toes, almost daring them to doubt her flexibility and strength. She looked like she might break into a cartwheel any second.


Her liveliness finally eased some of their worry.Julia's tension faded just a bit, though she still clung to her motherly concern. "I should have come to fetch you myself. It's too risky for someone your age to go home by yourself."


The comment almost made Grace laugh. In truth, she was probably the last person in the world who needed protecting.
Switching gears, she threw out a question to shift the conversation. "So tell me-how did you two know to find me here?"


Julia, easily sidetracked, started to answer. But before she could finish, Colton made his entrance,freshly bandaged from his own treatment.


"It was Colton!" Julia blurted out in relief. "He told me what happened-if not for him, I'd have had no idea where to look. You really gave me a scare this time,sweetheart..." Her voice shook, threatening tears all over again.


A flicker of surprise crossed Grace's face. What business did Colton have talking with her parents?


Elite families often crossed paths, sharing connections through business, tradition, or even arranged marriages-none of that was out of the ordinary.


Still, Grace eyed Colton warily, unable to shake a wave of suspicion.

Wearing a look of harmless innocence, Colton explained, "While you were tending to your cuts,your mom's calls kept lighting up your phone. I went ahead and answered, thinking she'd want to know what was going on." He glanced over, his face full of apology. "Honestly, I wasn't snooping.I just thought it'd be worse not to answer her."



Julia broke into a bright smile, brushing off any concern. "No need to say sorry! Without your help,we'd never have known about the accident. If anything,I'm grateful."


Grace could only sigh, lips curving into a faint,bewildered smile.


In a quiet tone, she leaned closer to Colton and whispered, "Did you really have to tell my mom?I was on my way home anyway-she wouldn't have found out."


Telling her parents had never been part of the plan.Grace intended to slip home quietly, dab on her own custom ointment, and wake up the next morning with barely a mark left behind. No one would have guessed a thing.


A soft laugh escaped Colton as he leaned closer,lowering his voice to a private whisper. "I thought it'd be nice if your folks realized you and I... share a connection. Who knows, maybe you'll give me a proper introduction soon."


Grace stared, taken aback. "Wait-what's that supposed to mean?" The families were familiar with each other already, so what was the point in introducing him to her folks?


Meanwhile, Julia took in the sight of Grace and Colton murmuring together and saw something entirely different.


She gave Rodger a nudge, whispering,"Honey,look at those two... Aren't they just perfect? They seem so close-maybe there's already something going on between them!"



A fierce blush shot across Grace's cheeks."Mom!It's not like that. We're not dating!"
Rodger's posture stiffened at once, concern flickering in his eyes. "That's right. Girls your age shouldn't be thinking about romance just yet."


Colton could hardly hide his amusement as the scene played out. Everything was falling neatly into place. Instead of bristling at Rodger's sternness, he wore a smile.


"You have a point, Mr. Holden. Grace should be focused on life's bigger adventures before she even considers dating."
###Chapter 83 A Command He'd Regret





Rodger's suggestion met with immediate acceptance from Colton, who understood that Grace's time as a student was drawing to a close.


Whether she was finalizing her plans for college or not,she was never one to pour all her focus into textbooks. Academics alone never satisfied her restless mind. Secrets trailed in her wake,and her talents stretched far beyond school walls.


Soon enough, the day would come when Grace stepped out of academia and into the wider world,and Colton's predictions would be set in motion.


Julia leaned in with approval. "That's just it, Colton.Grace is young and impressionable. The last thing l want is for her to fall under the sway of the wrong crowd. If you have the chance, do me the favor of watching over her," she said, trusting Colton's judgment far more than her own sons'.
Grace's prospects would be well-guarded if Colton stood watch; no sensible man would dare cross that line.


"You have my word, Mrs. Holden. I'll see to it personally," Colton replied, calm and certain. There was no way he'd let any man get close to Grace.


Grace wanted to object, thinking that her mother's standards for "reliable" guardianship were questionable at best.


Nightfall crept in, and with a few parting words,Rodger and Julia gathered Grace and set off, leaving Colton behind.


The family had barely turned the corner when Dominick slipped from the shadows, his presence quiet but sure. "Sir, I've uncovered that those behind today's incident are connected to the higher-ups."


A sharp glint entered Colton's eyes. "Which side-southern or northern?"



Only the true powerbrokers could orchestrate
something like this, and Colton knew it.


Dominick looked away, feeling a bit awkward.
"Honestly... I haven't been able to confirm that yet."


Colton, however, had already put the pieces together. The supposed divide between north and south was more smoke than fire; in reality, they all answered to the same country.


That never stopped ambitious souls from splintering into rival camps, each one unable to share power for long.


In the end, none of it mattered to Colton. He was already convinced the old man from the southern faction was behind the trouble.


"If that's the case, there's no point keeping the research institute open at Frostveil Mountain," Colton said,his tone resolute.


Dominick hesitated, unsure if he'd heard right. "You mean...?"


A cold light glinted in Colton's eyes. "The southern
faction is cultivating all kinds of plants up there,isn't it? Wipe them out. I want them to regret crossing me."


The thought left Dominick uneasy. He couldn't help but offer a warning. "Word is, those plants belong to the female genius of the southern faction.Destroying them might cause an uproar."


People in power held her in high regard, and making an enemy of her was asking for trouble that lasted a lifetime.



Rumor had it she loved collecting rare things-strange plants, exotic insects, and even venomous snakes. Stories went around that anyone who ended up on her bad side never met a happy ending.


A dismissive smile played at Colton's lips. "Let her raise hell. I hope she does. The more she resents me,the better," he replied, never realizing that one day he would regret ever issuing that command.


He figured the only/ way to unmask that woman was to push her buttons until she revealed her true identity.


Any information about her had been carefully concealed by the southern faction, and every attempt to dig deeper had come up empty.


A respectful nod from Dominick signaled he understood. "Right away, sir," he replied, then slipped out to carry out the orders.






Meanwhile, at the Holden residence, it was already past dinner time. Johnny and James still lingered on the living room sofa, having waited for everyone to return.



Watching his family file in, Johnny immediately noticed that Grace looked perfectly fine, not a hair out of place, and it made him wonder if their parents had been duped by her antics once again.


He shot her a skeptical look. "Wasn't it said you were in a car crash? You look just fine to me," he remarked, his voice edged with disdain as he eyed her immaculate clothes.


"You had Mom and Dad running all over town,thinking something terrible happened. All that panic for nothing," he muttered, not hiding his irritation.


Julia, however, missed the tone entirely. "Oh, Grace,you should have seen how anxious Johnny was! He ran right over to check on you and nearly cried with relief," she responded, completely misunderstanding his sarcasm.



A twitch pulled at the corner of Grace's mouth. How did Julia always manage to mistake Johnny's biting remarks for genuine concern?


Johnny could barely contain his irritation at his mother's ability to twist every situation and almost let his frustration show.



From across the room, James finally broke his usual silence. "Now that we know everyone's all right, let's eat. You're probably all hungry."


Carrying the weight of being the oldest, James had a reserved nature and had begun taking on more responsibility, working closely with Rodger on family business.



Julia, beaming with pride, latched onto his words."See? James cares about you. He doesn't want anyone missing dinner. Let's all sit down together,"she said, convinced of her eldest son's reliability and warmth.



Johnny rolled his eyes at his mother's habit of making every remark about Grace, especially since James hadn't singled out anyone in particular.


He chose not to argue, instead trailing after the others as the family made their way to the dining table.


A sense of nostalgia washed over Julia as she realized how long it had been since the entire family had shared a meal.


"Having Grace at home brings such joy. Even James shows up for dinner more often these days," Julia remarked, her voice soft with sentiment.

James managed a gentle reply. "Of course. Family meals matter, especially when Grace is here," he said, his words warm, though his gaze remained distant, subtle, and unnoticed by most.
###Chapter 84 Not Sibling Care
The emotional toll of Grace's accident weighed heavily on Julia. Whether it was the shock or simply exhaustion from so many tears, she found herself drained by the end of dinner. She decided to wash up early and retreat straight to her room.


Nevertheless, she refused to let her nightly ritual slide. Bringing a mug of warm milk to Grace before bed had become almost sacred-a habit rooted in her belief that her daughter, still too thin from her difficult years before joining their family, needed every ounce of nourishment and care.


Evenings always saw Julia knocking on Grace's door,milk in hand and a ready excuse to share stories or simply linger together a bit longer.


Fatigue,however,left Julia spent tonight.


Passing the baton, she asked her son to deliver both the milk and a bit of brotherly warmth-to use this
moment to grow closer to Grace.


James, ever the dutiful and thoughtful son, never hesitated when his mother called on him. He gave a quick nod and set off down the hall.


It wasn't long before he stood outside Grace's room,mug in hand, tapping softly at the door.


"Come in."



Seeing James enter instead of Julia caught Grace off guard. That nightly ritual of milk and quiet conversation was Julia's domain, a rare, cherished moment they both looked forward to.


James crossed the threshold, offering a gentle smile."Mom's wiped out tonight, so she asked me to take over milk duty," he explained, his tone calm and kind,his eyes soft with warmth.


Yet, behind the kindness, Grace detected something else-a faint but unmistakable sense of distance.



She'd sensed it for a while now. Outwardly, James acted as loving as any brother, his gestures echoing
their parents' affection, but something always felt held back. His gaze, steady and quiet, never quite lost that subtle reserve.


Perhaps it was all just a performance for Julia's sake,James putting on the mask of the attentive older brother because that was what his parents expected to see. Or maybe, at his core, he was simply the kind of person who kept a subtle barrier between himself and the world.


Grace found herself leaning toward the former,suspecting that genuine affection wasn't part of the equation for James.


Honestly, she couldn't blame him. She was still the newcomer here, and expecting him to treat her like real family right away would have been naive.


She lifted the mug with a small nod. "Thanks,James." The words were simple, but polite.


A sip brought comfort-Julia's careful touch evident in every warm, familiar swallow.

James quietly observed, eyes catching on the milk's pale mark on the edge of her lip-a fleeting glimpse of innocence, making her seem much younger than she usually did.


For a heartbeat, the urge to reach over and wipe it away nearly won out, but awkwardness crept in, and he pulled back.


There she sat, swaddled in pink pajamas, her hair damp and curling softly over her shoulders-a gentle domestic scene.


He weighed the idea of offering to heIp dry her hair,the words on the tip of his tongue. The part he was meant to play was obvious, but stepping into it felt somehow false. Better to stay silent than force a gesture that wasn't real.


Grace sat quietly, as unbothered by the hush as ever,but she could tell James was uncomfortable with the stillness. Determined to keep the peace in the Holden household, she considered breaking the silence, hoping to ease whatever tension lingered between them.
Oddly enough, she never experienced this kind of strained silence whenever Colton was nearby. Even in wordless moments, his presence felt easy-natural,like breathing.


Yet with James, and truthfully with most people, that comfortable feeling just never seemed to settle in.


Eventually, James broke the hush. "Go ahead and finish your milk. Then get to bed early. You've got classes in the morning."


Grace responded with quiet courtesy, "Alright. You should get some rest too. Work comes early. Good night." She always tried to mirror politeness, still hoping to carve out her own place in this family.


He gave her a brief nod, turning to leave-then stopped short, seemingly on impulse. Reaching for the towel tossed over the chair, he set it gently atop her wet hair.


"You really shouldn't wash your hair so late," James scolded, keeping his tone soft. "And make sure to dry it off next time, or you'll wind up sick." With that,
he slipped out of her room.


For a moment, Grace paused, rubbing the towel into her hair, a flicker of surprise lighting her face.


Just now, she'd caught something unfamiliar in his gaze-an absence of the usual distance, maybe even a hint of warmth.


Was it possible he'd changed his mind about her? Or had she been reading him wrong from the very start?


Grace never wasted energy obsessing over questions that had no clear answers. Letting go of uncertainties was one of her quiet strengths; she never saw the point in tying herself up with needless worry.


Nevertheless, she reached for the hair dryer,diligently drying her hair before climbing under the covers for the night.


Meanwhile, in the house, James had barely stepped into the hallway before being grabbed and yanked sideways into the next room.
Johnny,waiting just outside his own door, was the culprit. His grip was firm and his glare sharper than usual. "James, what's with you suddenly acting so friendly toward her?"


Sharing a wall made these late-night ambushes all too easy.


With a steady voice, James replied, "She's part of our family now. That's what Mom wants, and I'm just following her lead. Why does it bother you if I treat her kindly?"


Patience laced James's words as he tried to bridge the gap with his younger brother. "You might not be Grace's biggest fan, but she's always respectful and never gives anyone trouble. There's no harm in showing her a bit of sibling care."


Johnny cut right through the explanation, saying,"Cut it out. I've watched you. That's not how someone looks at a real sister."



For a split second, something complicated flickered in James's expression-something too fast to pin down.



"Getting used to someone new in the family isn't automatic," James admitted, voice turning earnest as he slipped into his big brother role. "Still, it's up to us to make her feel like she belongs. That's what I'm going to do-and you should try,too."
###Chapter 85 Adrianna's Glowing
Johnny found himself wondering if he truly understood James anymore.


There had been a time when he was certain they were close, their small age gap making Johnny feel as though he knew everything about James.


Now, he could not shake the feeling that he was staring at someone completely unfamiliar.


Was it possible that James had fallen under Grace's spell too, just like their parents had?


Not long ago, Johnny was convinced that he and James were the only ones in sync within the family.Was he wrong?


"James, don't tell me you're another one who's fallen for Grace's act. Why should I have to treat her like a sister when even Gianna never got that title? And another thing-Mom actually gave her the special
mug. The one you just brought in was supposed to be for me and Mom!" he blurted out.



James heard his brother's frustration and simply shook his head, finding Johnny's behavior more childish than ever. Arguing about a mug seemed completely ridiculous to him.


"Just give it a rest. Like Mom said, we're supposed to be one big family." James spoke those words to Johnny, though it sounded like he was reminding himself too.


He finished what he had to say and walked out,unwilling to waste more time bickering with Johnny.


"Yeah right, as if I care about playing happy family with her. Grace is way too sneaky," Johnny muttered to himself, even though James was gone.


There was never a moment when Johnny truly liked Grace. He always felt like her presence left him on the outside of his own family.


The one thing he refused to forgive was how she
tried to come between him and Beatrice, making it sound like Beatrice was seeing some older man! The idea seemed impossible to him.


The more he dwelled on it, the more agitated he became, so Johnny reached for his phone and sent Beatrice a message, hoping she would reassure him.


Even after waiting quite a while, he received no reply from her. He assumed she had probably already gone to sleep, since she always stuck to her bedtime schedule.


At that very moment, however, Beatrice was resting in another man's arms.


Her parents barely paid attention to her, wrapped up in their own concerns, so they never questioned where she went or what she did. Things were much different for Johnny, who grew up under strict rules at home.







As the days passed, all the seniors became completely absorbed in preparing for the SATs,pouring their energy into this single pursuit.


With so much pressure in the air, only a small handful seemed calm and at ease.



A wave of happiness washed over Adrianna today.


The dark mark on her face, which doctors once claimed could never be removed, had vanished entirely.


Grace took one look and offered a nod of satisfaction. "That's impressive. The treatment worked even faster than I expected.It's half a month early."


Clearly, Adrianna had followed every instruction closely, and that effort paid off with such amazing results.



Gratitude filled Adrianna's voice as she squeezed Grace's hand. "Grace, I can't thank you enough. If it weren't for your help, I wouldn't feel as confident as l do now."
For a while now, that dark mark had been fading, and that alone had lifted her spirits.


This morning, when she woke to see her skin clear and glowing, a burst of pure joy ran through her.


Beauty meant a great deal to Adrianna, so she could not help but feel deeply grateful and thrilled.


"Try not to worry about how you look. You have a beautiful soul. You know, there's beauty everywhere,but finding someone with a beautiful soul is rare. Just believe in yourself," Grace explained.


Of everyone in the class, Adrianna stood out as Grace's dearest friend, and seeing her this happy made Grace feel truly delighted.


"Maybe so, but I owe you so much. If there's ever a day you need anything, I'll be there right away!"Adrianna said, her voice full of genuine gratitude,secretly thinking she would do almost anything for Grace. Even if it meant blurring the lines between friendship and something more.
Grace just laughed it off and waved her hand. "You don't need to make a big deal out of it."


Honestly, compared to treating Colton's serious condition, helping Adrianna with a mark feIt like a minor favor.


Her thoughts drifted to Colton again. For reasons she could not explain, he kept finding his way into her mind.



She gave her head a quick shake, determined to push thoughts of him away.


A voice rang out, surprised and loud. "Wait, did Adrianna really lose that giant mark?"


Someone else chimed in, "How did she pull it off?Without that mark, she's actually pretty, even prettier than Beatrice!"



"Looks like she didn't just lose that mark. Her skin's so much clearer and brighter. She's glowing now!"


Many classmates had been watching Adrianna's progress quietly, noticing every little change.

Now that her skin looked so healthy and the ugly mark was gone, the change seemed more impressive than anything a surgeon could do.


Charles could not help but notice how different Adrianna looked, too.


News traveled quickly, and once the girls in the class realized Grace was behind the transformation, all of them wanted to know her secret.


After all, almost everyone wanted to feel beautiful.
###Chapter 86 Becoming Popular

Whispers and curious glances had swirled around for ages before a girl finally found the nerve to step up to Grace. "Hey, Grace... where did you get that spot-fading skincare? Would you mind sharing the name?|saw how well it worked on Adrianna."


Grace met the question directly. "That's actually a homemade formula-a family secret. You won't find it on any store shelf."


It was a blend she'd invented herself, something she wasn't planning to share widely.


A flicker of disappointment flashed across the girl's face, though she couldn't help herself from trying again. "Well... could I maybe buy some from you?picked up way too many sunspots on my last trip,and nothing I tried seems to help."


This time, Grace responded without hesitation,"Sure,I can make you a jar."
Not expecting such an easy yes, the girl was left blinking, her prepared pitch suddenly unnecessary.Her surprise melted into a bright grin. "That's wonderful! Just let me know the price and I'll send you the money right now!"


At this school, nearly every student either had deep pockets or a sharp mind, and most had both.


Draped in luxury brands, most of these students simply assumed that Grace's skincare must be both high-quality and within their budgets-everyone seemed eager to get their hands on a bottle.



"Grace, count me in too! Could you make one for me?"



"I'm looking for something to help brighten my complexion and clear up some breakouts. Is there anything in your collection for that?"



Before long, the group treated Grace as if she ran her own little beauty shop, crowding around with requests and wish lists.
None of them realized that Grace's formulas were, in fact, Dr. Q's masterpieces-priceless creations in the world of skincare.



Put up for auction, these products could easily rake in millions, far beyond what any typical student allowance could handle.



But in the spirit of friendship, Grace surprised her classmates. "Don't worry about paying. We're al friends here, so these are on the house."


Her classmates received the offer as a gesture of goodwill-a thoughtful present rather than a transaction.


At first, a few wondered if they'd misheard, but when Grace's words were confirmed, delight swept through the group.


Even those who had once kept their distance or harbored quiet doubts about Grace now found themselves warming up, drawn in by her kindness.


Adrianna couldn't help but notice the change,

genuinely surprised at how easily the class atmosphere shifted to one of friendliness and acceptance-and she felt a quiet pride in the moment.



There was no denying it: the beauty products Grace shared worked miracles, delivering results that other brands couldn't even promise.


Within days of trying Grace's skincare, the girls in her class saw their reflections change-clearer,brighter,with not a single side effect to worry about.


This was worlds apart from the store-bought brands,which too often left users with lingering problems.


It didn't take long for word to travel; soon, stories of the "Grace effect" were circulating through every hallway and lighting up the school's online forums.


Previously, most of these girls blended into the background, never quite standing out for their looks.


Some were blessed with good bone structure but plagued by stubborn skin; others had clear skin but forgettable features, while a handful had both but always seemed to fade from memory.


Grace's gifts changed all that. Now, their complexions glowed, their personal style sharpened,and they walked with quiet self-assurance.


Adrianna's transformation stood out the most. Once written off as the class's least attractive, she lost the dark mark on her face and emerged as a genuine beauty, drawing comparisons to Beatrice for charm and poise, though still falling a bit short of Gianna.


As friendships with Grace warmed, so did the girls'willingness to listen. They eagerly followed her tips on clothing and hair, their appearances leveling up with each suggestion.


Confidence followed. It showed in the way they moved, the way they laughed, the way they met the world directly.


Grace quickly found herself the center of attention,admired and adored by nearly everyone in her year.
Her positive influence didn't go unnoticed;classmates who benefited from her help cherished her all the more.


Even students outside her class felt pangs of envy,wishing they could be close to Grace.



Soon enough, the demand became too great to ignore. Through friends, classmates, or shy notes slipped into her hand, beauty-obsessed girls from all over campus started asking if there was any way to buy Grace's magical creations.



Turning down a business opportunity wasn't in Grace's nature-she decided there was no reason not to profit from her talents.



For students from other classes, though, her price tags weren't the generous deals she'd given her classmates. Instead, she set rates that reflected the true value of her formulas-numbers more suited to luxury boutiques than school hallways.


The jaw-dropping prices left some girls reeling.
Sticker shock set in. Who could actually pay so much just for skincare?


A few were desperate enough for flawless skin to scrape together the money, but most quickly gave up after hearing the cost.


Lizzie complained to anyone who'd listen. "That bumpkin Grace Miller claims she made those creams herself, but look at what she's charging! Six figures for a small jar-she might as well be robbing us in broad daylight." Secretly, she wanted nothing more than to get her hands on a jar.


Gianna, still smarting from her own recent failures,rolled her eyes and offered advice with forced indifference. "She has always had a knack for scheming. Just let her be. You should focus on your grades and getting into a good university."


Since Terry's last visit, Gianna's usual self-assurance had all but vanished, replaced by a constant undercurrent of nerves.


Meanwhile, Ellie was watching her own career slip through her fingers. About all she could do was push Gianna to keep her head down and aim for the top universities in the country.


Otherwise, all the energy she'd poured into Gianna would have been wasted.

###Chapter 87 What Matters Is Who You Are
Lizzie's real aim was to stir up Gianna, hoping she'd explode at Grace for the outrageous pricing.


Gianna,however, wasn't about to take the bait. She prided herself on her flawless skin and her upbringing as part of the Holden family, and she saw no point in tossing away good money on Grace's fancy concoctions.


Landing a spot at her top-choice university was her priority-she could always settle old scores with Grace once she'd secured her future.


Realizing that Gianna remained perfectly composed,Lizzie had to set her plans aside for now.


Meanwhile, Beatrice found herself growing increasingly anxious.


Fear crept in as she wondered if Grace had

uncovered her secret relationship with that much older man. She'd planned to play it safe, but lately,the man's attention and the gifts had dried up.



Depending on Johnny wasn't much help either. He hadn't started working yet, and every penny he spent still had to pass through his parents' hands.


Their rules about money bordered on the absurd.Johnny's allowance was a fraction of what Grace got -hardly enough to fund Beatrice's tastes.


If Beatrice hadn't met Julia and seen the uncanny resemblance between mother and son, she might have suspected Johnny was the one who'd been adopted.


With Johnny's limited resources, Beatrice's lavish habits were in jeopardy. For now, he would have to be her last resort.



She couldn't help but notice that those long nights spent keeping her sugar daddy entertained had started to show on her skin. The glow she once had was gone, replaced by a sallow, tired look-no wonder the man was losing interest.


It was clear to Beatrice that she needed Grace's famous skincare now more than ever.


Once, she would have laughed at the idea that Grace could offer anything of value. But after watching Adrianna's dramatic transformation-witnessing the former laughingstock become one of the school's beauties-Beatrice found herself unable to argue with the results.



"Leave this to me, Beatrice. There's no way she'll have the guts to humiliate you with a flat-out rejection." Chloe Robinson-Beatrice's loyal sidekick and regular beneficiary of her generosity-didn't hesitate to take the lead.



Without wasting time, Chloe tracked Grace down.


"You're just out to scam people, aren't you? Selling some random, unapproved cream for an arm and a leg-who do you think you are?"


Grace barely glanced her way. "Nobody's forcing you to buy. In fact, I might refuse even if you change your mind."


"Careful. I could easily file a complaint. You're pushing unregulated stuff and breaking the law."Chloe tried to play tough, hoping a threat might get her somewhere.


Grace just gave a small, unconcerned shrug. "Go ahead. All my products are fully certified-top-tier quality,in fact."


The truth was, her formulas had been crafted for the wives of presidents and visiting royalty. If Chloe ended up with one, it would be pure charity.


"You-" Chloe faltered, caught off guard by how unshakable Grace remained. She'd expected panic,maybe even some groveling, Instead, Grace seemed untouchable-cold and unbothered, not budging an inch.


Clearly, Chloe had misjudged her opponent.


"If it's out of your price range, just admit it. There's 
no need to throw around threats or drag Grace's name through the mud." Adrianna had always been the quiet one, rarely drawing attention. Yet with Grace by her side, she'd found a boldness that left no room for bullies, even when her voice trembled,she stood her ground.


A harsh laugh escaped Chloe. "You? Acting tough with me, you pauper? Just because you scrubbed up alright, you suddenly think you can play in my league?"


The very idea that Adrianna-once the overlooked,awkward girl-now dared to talk back was enough to make Chloe seethe.


Grace regarded Chloe with a raised brow, her stare cool and faintly amused. "Did you just call Adrianna poor? Are you really that clueless?"


She'd taken the time to learn about Adrianna's background. Three generations of military service, a direct descendant of a general, and both parents currently holding high-ranking posts-Adrianna's roots ran deep.
Yet here was Chloe, dismissing her as some penniless nobody.


That was what happened when people never looked beyond the surface.


Chloe gave a scoff, trying to hold onto her confidence. "Obviously, she's got nothing. Or did you think she was some trust fund princess? Is that wvhy you're clinging to her now?"


It was clear Chloe thought she'd figured it all out-that Grace must have befriended Adrianna for status or money.


She wasn't above snooping, either. After helping out with admin work, Chloe had peeked at more than one student's file.


Other than Charles Pearson, most students'backgrounds weren't impressive.


Her first attempt at social climbing had been with Charles, but he brushed her off without a second glance. Once it became clear that Johnny was completely wrapped up in Beatrice, she wasted no time latching onto Beatrice instead.


When it came to Adrianna, though? Chloe had seen her student record herself-nothing impressive in the background column. She believed Adrianna sat at the bottom of the school's unofficial pecking order, just an ordinary kid whose spot at Briskvale High was likely earned through sheer hard work.


Adrianna's nerves showed as she rushed to speak up. "Grace isn't like that," she insisted, glancing anxiously in Grace's direction.


Growing up in a household led by decorated officers,Adrianna's life was marked by discipline and humility.Her family's achievements were never something to flaunt, and she'd learned early on to keep her heritage in the background. She wanted friendships based on genuine connection, not on status or background.


Her mother's words rang in her mind: "Real friends love you for you, not for your last name. Just a couple of true friends are enough for a lifetime."

If Grace was going to feel ashamed by her, Adrianna figured it was better to be upfront.


After all, Grace was the one person who'd helped her shed old insecurities and find her sense of self-a friend like no other.


Grace's lips curved in a gentle smile. "That's right,"she answered softly. "What matters is who you are,not your family tree."


She knew better than anyone how little background should matter-her own beginnings were in an orphanage, and she'd never judge someone from a good,honest family.
###Chapter 88 Romance Could Wait
Grace's soft smile, paired with her gentle words, sent a comforting warmth right through Adrianna.


A rush of affection made Adrianna's heart skip. If she wasn't careful, she'd end up idolizing Grace outright.


Chloe rolled her eyes at the whole display, not bothering to hide her annoyance. "Wow, the friendship here is so moving I might cry. Listen,Beatrice is set on getting that beauty cream. If you refuse her, Johnny's going to be furious, and life with the Holdens will turn ugly for you."


At that, Grace arched an eyebrow. "Turn ugly for me?You do realize, right? My mom absolutely dotes on me-she's never been one to favor sons. I get spoiled far more than Johnny ever has."


In the past, Grace might have doubted her place,but now there was no question: Julia treated her like a little princess, showering her with love and luxuries.
She continued, a sly edge in her voice, "Didn't you catch Johnny's latest complaint to Beatrice? My mom's a platinum member at every major designer house.The shoes, the bags, the clothes she buys for me-they're all limnited edition, bought in sets. Johnny only gets that kind of attention at Christmas and his birthdays."


When it came to women like Chloe, nothing worked better than highlighting the exact things they longed for most.


Fuming, Chloe let out a huff. "You spoiled brat," she spat, her jealousy plain as day, but she had no choice but to stalk off.


Just as she turned to leave, Grace's voice rang out,cold and clear. "And Chloe, you might want to tell Beatrice this: if she betrayed Johnny, she'd better be ready for payback. Don't say | didn't give fair warning."


"What are you implying? Beatrice would never betray Johnny!" Chloe stopped in her tracks, caught off guard. She tried to sound indignant, but the defensiveness in her voice betrayed her. "Quit trying to start trouble between them!"


Grace just lifted her shoulders in a small shrug,opting to let the conversation drop.


The gesture only made Chloe more certain that Grace was out to cause drama. She shot Grace one last scowl before storming off.


As Chloe's figure disappeared down the hall, Grace's mind started to turn over what she'd just seen.


Apparently, Beatrice's involvement with an older man was something even Chloe didn't know about.


Then again, what girl would ever confess to her friend that she had found herself a sugar daddy?


In any case, Grace doubted Chloe would prove loyal if things got ugly. Their friendship struck her as shallow, more convenient than genuine.


After Chloe was gone, Adrianna stepped closer and said softly, "Grace, there's something I haven't told you. The truth is... my parents aren't ordinary
  workers. They're actually in the military..."


Words tangled on her tongue, and for a moment she simply fell silent, unsure how to explain without saying too much.


Because of the sensitive nature of her parents' work -always shrouded in secrecy-she was bound by more than just family loyalty. Even she was kept in the dark about the true details of their assignments.


Grace caught the hesitation and responded with easy reassurance, "You don't have to explain anything to me. I'm not like Chloe or Beatrice-I don't get hung up on background or status. All I want is for you to stay yourself, and for our friendship to stay solid." Power and poverty meant little in Grace's eyes; she'd met people from every walk of life, and none of it ever changed what really mattered to her.


"Grace,you really are the best! Honestly, if I were a guy, l'd propose to you on the spot!" Adrianna threw her arms around Grace, utterly delighted, the picture of a devoted fan.
There was truth in Grace's words-so long as they stayed true to themselves, nothing could threaten the bond they shared. All those other details faded into insignificance.


Grace paused, a hint of mischief in her eyes. "Well,technically, we're not old enough for marriage yet."


Romantic feelings for women had never sparked in her,and there wasn't a man on her radar either.


Right now, her mind was set on her life and goals-romance could wait.






Meanwhile, Chloe was fuming elsewhere. "Isn't it ridiculous how full of herself Grace Miller has become? First, she refuses to sell her beauty creams for a fair price, then she tries to slander you and wedge herself between you and Johnny! Honestly,she has no shame. People say she's always seen with strange men in flashy cars-who knows what she's realy up to? And now she dares accuse you of betraying Johnny!"
Chloe poured out her loyalty to Beatrice, but her words only made Beatrice's anxiety grow sharper.


Already uneasy from guilt, Beatrice couldn't take Grace's threats lightly. Waiting around for disaster wasn't an option-she needed to act.


"Forget her," Beatrice retorted, trying to sound confident. "I'll talk to Johnny myself. If I play it right,he'll make sure Grace coughs up that cream. Once that's done, you'll get your share too."


Hearing Beatrice's promise lit up Chloe's face. She wasted no time in sliding over and looping her arm through Beatrice's. "You're amazing, Beatrice. You always look out for me."


Beneath it all, Chloe was desperate for her own taste of beauty.


"That's what friends are for-I'll always have your back." Beatrice assured her, sounding proud and self-assured.



There was no doubt in Beatrice's mind.With Johnny so firmly under her sway, she believed getting what she wanted would be a breeze.


As soon as lunch rolled around, Beatrice wasted no time bringing up the subject with Johnny.


"Wait, you want Grace's skincare stuff?" Johnny blinked in surprise.


Sure, he understood the obsessian girls had with skincare-and he cared plenty about his own looks-but could Grace's concoctions really be worth all the hype?


He couldn't help but wonder how her products had become such a craze throughout the school.
###Chapter 89 Stay Away From Johnny
"Hey, did you see how Adrianna Walsh got rid of that dark mark on her face? l've been up all night studying, and my skin's been acting up. Can you ask your sister if I could get some of her stuff too?"


Beatrice knew how to get her way with Johnny. A little charm, a sweet tone-he usually gave in without much resistance. Today should be no different.


But to her shock, Johnny replied without hesitation,"No,I can't."


Beatrice's smile faltered.


Johnny must've sensed the tension and felt he was too blunt. It was rare for him to feel uneasy. "Don't get me wrong, Beatrice," he said quickly. "I just don't think you should take Grace's products too seriously.She's always mixing random stuff without any clear source. It's not exactly... safe. What if it messes up your skin in a few weeks? It's not worth the risk."
Beatrice opened her mouth to push back-she had made a promise to Chloe and didn't want to seem unreliable.


Johnny had a point. If her face broke out or worse,it'd be a disaster. No apology would fix that.


"My mom's got memberships with all the major skincare brands," Johnny added, trying to soften the blow. "I'll get you something better. Sound good?"Since it was the first time Johnny had ever turned Beatrice down, guilt crept in quickly, and he rushed to make it up to her.



In his mind, asking Grace for anything was complicated. He didn't want to owe her, and he definitely didn't want to deal with his mother's suspicions if she caught wind of this.


His family didn't know he was dating, and the thought of their probing questions made him uneasy.


Beatrice perked up. "Johnny, you're the best." Even if she only got a little at a time, luxury skincare from top brands was more than most girls could dream of.

She couldn't complain.


Johnny relaxed a little when he saw her smile again,but deep down, he felt drained. This was what girls liked,right? Being spoiled?


After lunch, Beatrice claimed she needed a nap and parted ways with Johnny. In reality, she had another man to meet.



Most people would think this could be exhausting,sneaking off between classes like this-but to her, it was thrilling. After all, being spoiled by rich men of all kinds and showered with gifts was the kind of life most average-looking girls could only dream about.


Beatrice was not able to rest, and by afternoon, the effects of skipping rest caught up with her.


The next class was PE-thankfully. She could fake feeling unwell and sneak off to the infirmary to rest.


She was halfway there when she saw a face she didn't want to see.



It was Grace.

In her memory, Grace always acted like she enjoyed being on her own. Maybe it was because no one had the patience to handle her attitude, let alone try to be her friend.Beatrice had been wanting a face-to-face with Grace for a while, and now that the moment was here, she wasn't going to waste it.


"Why are you sitting here all alone? Where's your sidekick, Adrianna?" Beatrice's tone was smug,confident that her opening jab would get under Grace's skin.


But Grace didn't flinch. She sat on a bench, still, eyes closed, like she hadn't heard a word.


Beatrice frowned, thinking maybe Grace had dozed off. She stepped closer, dropped the soft-girl act,and said sharply, "You don't have PE now. Sitting here like this, aren't you scared of getting a demerit for skipping class?"


Still, no response. Beatrice suddenly felt foolish, like she was talking to a statue.


"Are you deaf or what?!" she snapped, her voice
louder now, fueled by frustration. At last, Grace opened her eyes just a sliver.


"Are you dumb or something? I heard you barking the whole time like a stray. Does Johnny know you act like this?"



Beatrice's breath caught in her throat. So Grace had heard her all along and deliberately ignored her-just to make her squirm.


"You look like a madwoman," Grace said calmly,leaning back like she had all the time in the world.


"You've got some nerve insulting me! I'm warning you-l recorded all this. I'll show it to Johnny!"


"Be sure to include the part about which guy you were sweet-talking today. No sleep at night, no rest at noon, those dark circles are no joke."


"Shut your mouth!" Beatrice's heart skipped. How did Grace know that? Had she bugged her? It was uncanny-too specific to be a guess.


"You know I'm telling the truth." Grace's voice lost all sweetness. The calm, kind front she wore for the world had vanished. She chose who deserved it--and Beatrice didn't.



She looked at Beatrice with disdain. Johnny really deserved better.


"Slander me again without proof and I'll sue you for defamation!" Beatrice snapped, trying to sound tough,though her voice cracked a little at the end.


Grace tilted her head. "You really are gifted."Beatrice blinked. A compliment? She straightened slightly. Well, it wasn't a lie. She was talented.


But then Grace added, "You really have a talent for keeping your cool, even when your dirty little secret is out in the open. I warn you, stay away from Johnny.I couldn't care less about the rest of your sugar daddies."



Grace rarely got involved in things that weren't her business. She was known for being cold and distant.


Despite her intellect and eerie calm, she lacked certain emotional traits. Still, the Holden family had filled in those missing parts well enough-especially when it came to protecting what mattered.
###Chapter 90 Giving Her Something Real To Cry About
Grace's genes were anything but ordinary-a handpicked blend of the brightest and strongest the elite world had to offer.


From her earliest days, she outpaced other children by leaps and bounds, mastering skills before most could even talk.


Still, all those years working in the shadows for her country had turned her into more of a tool than a person, moving through life without a hint of emotion.



Joining the Holden family marked a turning point-now, she was wrapped in genuine affection. She became personal and human.


Beatrice's voice trembled as she stammered, "I...I haven't done anything! Quit making up stories! If you've got something on me, then prove it!"


But the more she turned it over in her mind,the more she convinced herself-Grace must be bluffing. If there were real evidence, Grace wouldn't waste time with threats. She'd have already exposed her to Johnny. Clearly, this was just a psychological play-a classic move to spook her into making a mistake.She'd never let herself be caught that easily.


"Fine then, bring out your evidence. I doubt it would matter-Johnny would take my word over yours any day," Beatrice retorted, her earlier nerves fading,arrogance taking root again.


Watching Grace keep her composure only fueled Beatrice's sense of triumph. Her smirk grew wider,convinced she'd seen right through the game.


With her usual hawk-likeattention, Grace noticed Johnny striding across the lawn, heading straight for them.



Talk about timing-he couldn't have shown up at a better moment.  Beatrice had been itching for an excuse to put Grace in her place for ages.


"If you'd just stayed out of things, Grace, I wouldn't have wasted a second on a nobody like you. You're just a stray with no real family. Honestly, you don't even belong in my world! But since you decided to poke the bear... well, whatever happens next is on you."


In a flash, she lifted her hands and delivered two dramatic, echoing slaps to her own cheeks.


Grace stared, taken aback.


Was this the latest twist-threats giving way to a solo slap show?


A voice cut through her thoughts, and everything clicked into place.


"Beatrice? What are you doing out here?" Johnny's voice rang out, worry laced through every syllable.


The moment he'd heard Beatrice wasn't feeling well,he'd made a beeline for the infirmary, only to spot her here by a bench and come rushing over.


But as he drew closer and caught sight of her reddened cheeks, he stopped in his tracks."Beatrice...what happened to your face?"


Instantly, Beatrice's eyes filled with tears, her voice trembling with expertly practiced distress. "Johnny...thank goodness you're here. I don't know what I did wrong-your sister just attacked me for no reason...I only wanted to talk, that's all."


"Grace did this to you?!" Disbelief clouded Johnny's face, his features hardening as he tried to process the accusation.



With a trembling voice, Beatrice continued, "| just thought... since she's your family, I should try to make peace. But she... she wouldn't even let me finish a sentence-"


Her words faded away, but the insinuation lingered heavily in the air.

 
"Grace, have you completely lost it? Who hits  someone out of nowhere like that?" Johnny's voice rang out in sharp accusation.


A sliver of doubt gnawed at the back of his mind-random violence didn't sound like Grace at all.


But loyalty had a funny way of clouding judgment,and with Beatrice looking so pitiful, heknew which side he'd take.



Before Grace could get a word in, she calmly lifted her arm and, with practiced ease, landed two stinging slaps right across Beatrice's cheeks.


The faint marks from earlier instantly flared into angry red welts, hot and throbbing.


Shocked into stillness, Beatrice could do nothing but gape, her face burning and swelling beneath the sudden blows.


Grace wasn't built like the average girl. Even holding back, her strikes left a memory Beatrice would feel for days.


"I didn't lay a finger on her before. But since she's so determined to pin the blame on me-and I can't prove otherwise-l figure I might as well live up to her story." A casual shrug accompanied Grace's words.She'd never tolerated being falsely accused. Rather than waste breath arguing, she'd rather make the accusation a fact and end the farce right then and there.


Beatrice pressed a trembling hand to her cheek,staring in disbelief. "Did you really just hit me?I can't believe you actually went through with it!"


Grace tilted her head, her voice dripping with mock cheer. "Weren't you just claiming I struck you for no reason? Now I'm only doing what I'm told. You ought to be grateful, honestly."


Usually, Grace kept to herself, but in that moment,she wielded her words like a blade, tearing into Beatrice without hesitation.


Johnny could only gape, frozen on the spot. Several seconds ticked by before Beatrice let out a pitiful whimper, tears beginning to spill, which finally snapped him out of his daze. He stepped forward, outrage coloring his tone."Grace, have you lost your mind? Why would you go after her like that? What did she ever do to deserve this?"



Grace offered a dismissive shrug. "I've already explained it. She hit herself, then tried to pin it on me.I just figured I might as well play along and give her something real to cry about."


Locking eyes with him, she watched his reaction.Her gaze held steady, cold and unblinking, as though daring him to challenge her version of the story.


He had been preparing a tirade, but when faced with that unflinching stare, the words dried up before they could leave his mouth.



A heavy silence lingered. He could do nothing but stare.



Grace's voice turned airy, almost indifferent."Whether you believe me or not, that's your call."With that, she spun on her heel and strode off,unaffected. The bell rang, signaling the end of class, and now a small crowd of students drifted past, pausing to watch the spectacle with wide-eyed curiosity.
###Chapter 91 Enemy Of Her Enemy





The ruckus quickly drew the attention of several students passing by.


Grace, Beatrice, and Johnny were all well-known figures at school, often the center of attention.


With the three of them now in a confrontation, it instantly became the subject of gossip, with students whispering and speculating about what was going on.


"|I swear I didn't slander her, Johnny. Don't you trust me?" Beatrice cried, tears streaming down her face,unfazed by the growing audience.


She had always been in the limelight and thrived on attention. Being ignored was far more unsettling for her.



What she hadn't anticipated was that Grace wouldn't follow the usual script. Beatrice had already delivered two slaps to herself, only to receive two more from Grace.



Talk about a streak of bad luck!


What made her blood boil even more was the fact that Johnny didn't slap Grace back, nor did he call her out in front of everyone.


"Don't cry. I believe you," Johnny said, trying to juggle his own frustration and confusion while attempting to soothe Beatrice. "There are too many eyes on us right now. Let's talk somewhere else."


With that, he gently took her hand and led her away.


Seeing that the main characters had left, the crowd of gossiping students quickly lost interest and began to scatter.


Only Gianna, who had been lurking quietly in a corner, and Lizzie, her ever-devoted sidekick,remained, unable to contain their buzz of excitement.


"Looks like Grace is making enemies left and right.Even Beatrice can't stand her," Lizzie commented with a smirk.

By now, nearly everyone in their grade knew that Beatrice's confident strut around campus was all thanks to Johnny's support.


Without his backing, considering her family background, she would probably still be on the same level as Grace, who came from an orphanage.


This thought stirred resentment and envy in Lizzie.She couldn't understand what Johnny saw in Beatrice. She was also attractive and came from a far more prestigious family, so why hadn't he ever noticed her?



"Well,this actually works in our favor. Like they say,the enemy of my enemy is my friend," Gianna said,clearly pleased by the situation.



"What are you getting at?" Lizzie asked, curious.


"I'm saying we are going to make a new friend,"Gianna replied.







In a quiet, deserted hallway, Johnny was gently trying to soothe Beatrice. "Don't cry, Beatrice. I know you have been wronged."


He softly pressed an ice pack to her cheek while speaking in a soothing tone. "When I get home tonight, I'll make sure she pays for this. I'll ask my mom to cut off her allowance."



"Really? But isn't your mom super fond of her?"Beatrice asked, still doubtful.


"No matter how much my mom likes her, she is still adopted. Do you think she means more than me, her own son?" Johnny said with smug confidence."I'll have my mom transfer all of Grace's allowance to me. She is only attending this school because my dad donated a lab building. Now that she is stirring up trouble, my mom will teach her a lesson. Our family is all about discipline over spoiling." Once I get the money, I'll buy you those new designer shoes.And didn't you say you have been eyeing those international-brand skincare products? I'll buy them for you!"


 
Johnny understood that Beatrice wasn't difficult to please. She loved shopping and being spoiled with gifts, so he figured he would just have to tighten his budget a bit to keep her happy.


Beatrice's eyes lit up at first, but she quickly composed herself and shook her head. "I don't want that. You have already gotten me so many things lately. It's more than enough."


"As long as you're happy, I can handle it," Johnny said sincerely.


"No, seriously. Just spending time with you, eating together, studying, and going shopping once in a while is all I need," Beatrice replied.


"Every girl enjoys shopping. I can't let you feel less special than anyone else," Johnny said instinctively.Deep down, he sensed that if he didn't treat her with gifts, he would have to work harder to keep her content.


Though he was still green and hadn't given it much thought, he assumed all girls were probably like that.


"Alright then... Thank you, Johnny. You're the best person in the world to me." Beatrice finally managed to smile through her tears.


Even though she hadn't managed to see Grace get punished on the spot, being pampered wvith luxury gifts from Johnny made for a satisfying consolation prize.


After finally calming her down, Johnny hurried off,called away by a teacher who needed him for something.


The moment he disappeared from view, Beatrice dropped her act. She lazily scrolled through her phone, replying to a few messages from admirers and tossing in a bit of harmless flirting before rising slowly and making her way back toward class.


But the second she rounded the corner, she came face-to-face with someone unexpected.


"Hi," Gianna greeted her first, her tone unusually.friendly.


Beatrice blinked, caught off guard. Gianna had always carried herself with an air of superiority and had never bothered to speak to her directly. What was she doing here now, initiating a conversation?


"Did you come looking for me?" Beatrice immediately suspected that this wasn't a random encounter.


"Yes, I wanted to talk to you about something,"Gianna replied smoothly.


"Is this about Grace?" Beatrice wasn't naive. In fact,she was quite sharp, and she immediately saw through Gianna's purpose.



Both Beatrice and Gianna were attractive and well-known at school. While Beatrice didn't quite measure up to Gianna in terms of status, the two had mostly kept their distance from one another.



But ever since Grace had transferred in, she had managed to steal their spotlight without even trying.


Beatrice was convinced Gianna resented Grace just as much as she did.



"You're right. I enjoy working with smart people,"Gianna said, nodding with a hint of approval."Then what do you want? Beatrice asked, arching an eyebrow.


"It's simple; I'm suggesting we work together. From this moment on, we could be friends," Gianna replied.
###Chapter 92 Julia Played Favorites
Long ago, Gianna never gave a second thought to anyone she deemed unworthy of her attention,always careful to guard her image and standing.


"That changed as Grace gradually stole her spotlight. She became eager to find an ally who also hated Grace.



These days, it seemed Grace had made it her mission to stir up trouble between Beatrice and Johnny, causing Beatrice's dislike for her to grow sharper with each passing day. Gianna believed the prospect of joining forces felt too good for Beatrice to pass up.


For Beatrice, it hardly mattered if the friendship with Gianna was shallow, as long as there was something in it for her.



Eventually, both girls found common ground and decided to work together.
 Plans were set: Gianna would grant Beatrice access to the Holden estate, opening doors to high society.In return, Beatrice would spread whispers and turn the tide against Grace.


Once the deal was sealed, each moved on as if nothing had happened.







Adrianna caught up with Grace, worry written on her face. "Grace, they're saying Beatrice's at it again,dragging your name through the mud. Is it true?"Not long before, she had overheard a pack of girls in the hallway, their conversation circling around Grace,Johnny,and Beatrice.


Rumors were swirling that Grace had a strained relationship with Johnny and was jealous of Beatrice.Some students even accused Grace of being insatiable.



Chloe,Beatrice's loyal companion, played ringleader,always ready with a fresh rumor to damage Grace's name. Unable to bite her tongue, Adrianna had confronted Chloe then and there, and their spat nded any hope of friendship.


Unfazed, Grace waved it off. "Let them gossip.I know what I'm doing, and I'll come out just fine."


Experience had taught her how to keep the upper hand. Laying out her strategies in silence, she preferred to wait until everything reached a boiling point before making her move.


Adrianna breathed easier. "That's a relief to hear,"she said with a soft smile.



A new kind of confidence had taken root in her.Grace had become someone she looked up to,pushing away her old insecurities and choosing, at last, to carve out her own happiness.


Grace shot her a look of warning. "You'd better stay alert. Chloe's got it out for you now, and she doesn't let things go easily."


Adrianna nodded with conviction. "I'll look after myself," she replied, genuinely uplifted by Grace's caring words. Her admiration for Grace only deepened in that moment.

It wasn't Johnny she feared-it was the possibility of upsetting Julia that truly bothered her.
